# Fault Localization: NFS Mount Disappears Due to Inode Revalidate Failure

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/linux--07cc49f6 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/linux--07cc49f6 (mirror of torvalds/linux)
- **Kernel Version**: 4.1.15
- **Difficulty**: expert
- **Category**: fault_localization
- **Subsystem**: File System
- **Component**: NFS / SunRPC

## Bug Report

**Bug ID**: 117651
**Summary**: Root NFS and autofs - mount disappears due to inode revalidate failed
**Regression**: Yes (works on 3.14.12, broken on 4.1.15)

After upgrading from 3.14.12 to 4.1.15 I've got strange behaviour with autofs.

It happens on diskless machine with root on NFS. There is autofs indirect mount on /storage, where NFS volumes are mounted on demand.

Everything mounts normally, but after mount expiration (during unmount) autofs mount disappears - that is, not only /storage/<volume> unmounts, but /storage is also unmounted. This happens quite often - usually on the very first expiration.

automount logs umount error in such cases.

Without autofs, mount/umount of the same NFS volume works correctly.

With NFS debug enabled, I've got following errors:

```
NFS reply getattr: -512
nfs_revalidate_inode: (0:15/6291480) getattr failed, error=-512
NFS: nfs_lookup_revalidate(/storage) is invalid
```

After inode revalidate failure all mounts on this inode are unmounted and so autofs mount disappears, while automount daemon itself continue to run.

tcpdump shows, that server replies to getattr without error, but client doesn't see this reply, and returning error instead.

I am ready to supply additional information.

## Task

You are a fault localization agent. Given the bug report above, your task is to identify the **exact source file(s)** and **function(s)/data structure(s)** in the Linux kernel source tree (at `/workspace`) that need to be modified to fix this bug.

You must:
1. Analyze the bug report to understand the symptoms and context
2. Search the kernel source code to identify the relevant subsystem and files
3. Narrow down to the specific file(s) and function(s)/data structure(s) that contain the bug or need modification
4. Write your findings to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json` in the following format:

```json
{
  "buggy_files": ["path/to/file.c"],
  "buggy_functions": ["function_or_struct_name"],
  "confidence": 0.8,
  "reasoning": "Brief explanation of why these locations are the fault"
}
```

**Important**: Paths should be relative to the kernel source root (e.g., `kernel/sched/core.c`, not `/workspace/kernel/sched/core.c`).

## Success Criteria

- [ ] Correctly identify the buggy file(s)
- [ ] Correctly identify the buggy function(s) or data structure(s)
- [ ] Write results to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json`
- [ ] Provide reasoning for the localization

Perfect! I found the bug! The issue is in the order of operations in `net/sunrpc/socklib.c` at lines 96-101. The variable `pglen` (page length to copy) is being decremented by `base` **BEFORE** `base` is adjusted by adding `xdr->page_base` and being masked. This causes `pglen` to be incorrectly calculated, leading to buffer underruns or overflow when copying RPC reply data.

Excellent! I have successfully identified the bug causing the NFS mount disappearance due to inode revalidate failure. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Fault Localization Summary

**Buggy File:** `net/sunrpc/socklib.c`  
**Buggy Function:** `xdr_partial_copy_from_skb()`  
**Confidence Level:** 0.95

### The Bug

In the `xdr_partial_copy_from_skb()` function at lines 96-101, there is an **order-of-operations bug** that causes incorrect calculation of the page length (`pglen`) when copying data from socket buffers to XDR buffers.

**Problematic Code:**
```c
if (base || xdr->page_base) {
    pglen -= base;        // LINE 97: Subtracts ORIGINAL base value
    base += xdr->page_base;  // LINE 98: Adjusts base
    ppage += base >> PAGE_CACHE_SHIFT;  // LINE 99: Advances page pointer
    base &= ~PAGE_CACHE_MASK;  // LINE 100: Masks to get offset within page
}
```

### The Issue

Line 97 subtracts the **original `base` value** from `pglen` before `base` is adjusted by adding `xdr->page_base` and masking. This causes `pglen` to have an **incorrect value** that doesn't match the actual offset within the first page of data.

The correct sequence should be:
1. Adjust `base` to the absolute offset (add `page_base`)
2. Calculate which page we start at
3. Mask `base` to get the offset **within** that page
4. **THEN** subtract this adjusted `base` from `pglen`

### Impact on the Bug Report

This order-of-operations bug causes:
- RPC reply buffers to be copied incompletely or incorrectly
- XDR decoding to fail when parsing the reply
- NFS `nfs_revalidate_inode()` to report "getattr failed" error (-512)
- During autofs mount expiration, this causes the /storage mount to disappear along with the mounted volumes
- The tcpdump shows the server replies successfully, but the client treat

This causes an incorrect pglen value to be used in the subsequent page copying loop, leading to buffer overrun/underrun when copying RPC reply data. Specifically, on line 97, 'pglen -= base' should occur AFTER lines 98-100 which adjust base to represent the actual offset within the first page. This causes an incorrect pglen value to be used in the subsequent page copying loop, leading to buffer overrun/underrun when copying RPC reply data. Specifically, on line 97, 'pglen -= base' should occur AFTER lines 98-100 which adjust base to represent the actual offset within the first page. The correct order should be: (1) add page_base to base, (2) calculate ppage offset, (3) mask base to get in-page offset, (4) THEN subtract the adjusted base from pglen. This bug causes RPC reply buffers to be incompletely or incorrectly copied, resulting in XDR decoding failures that manifest as 'getattr failed' errors in NFS inode revalidation, which is particularly problematic during autofs mount expiration when inode revalidation is triggered."
}
